C.2.3
Feature Extraction
function [EMDData] = feature_extraction(PrepData, databases, testCondition)
%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%
%
% DESCRIPTION: This function computes the EMD and DFT of each segment of
%
data, and then extracts features using cosine similarity measure.
%
% INPUT:
%
o PrepData: Struct containing each data segment for each subject for each
%
database after preprocessing
%
.(databases): ID of the database
%
.(subjectNo): ID of the subject
%
.(segmentNo): ID of the segment
%
.label: The label for the segment
%
.signal: The signal for the segment
%
.subjectID: The subject ID for the segment
%
.featureLabels: A vector including label conditions
%
o databases: The wanted database name(s)
132
==PAGE:158==
C.2. FUNCTIONS
Reference Algorithm
Implementation
%
o testCondition: Label condition
%
% OUTPUT:
%
o EMDData: Struct containing each data segment for each subject for each
%
database after preprocessing
%
.(databases): ID of the database
%
.(subjectNo): ID of the subject
%
.(segmentNo): ID of the segment
%
.label: The label for the segment
%
.subjectID: The subject ID for the segment
%
.featureLabels: A vector including label conditions
%
.simIMF: Similarity measure of a DFT of the signal and
%
a DFT of IMF
%
.simR: Similarity measure of a DFT of the signal and
%
a DFT of residue
%
% AUTHORS: Maria L. Sakhat (s154553) & Lena M. Nilsson (s153554)
%
%
% DATE CREATED: 28−09−20
% DATE MODIFIED: 14−10−20
%
%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%
%% EMD + DFT
% Defining parameters
alpha = 0.05;
beta = 0.02;
% Performing EMD for every segment
for db = 1:numel(fieldnames(PrepData))
database = databases{db};
for i = 1:numel(fieldnames(PrepData.(database)))
subjectNo = sprintf('subject%d',i);
for j = 1:numel(fieldnames(PrepData.(database).(subjectNo)))
segmentNo = sprintf('seg%d',j);
currentSig = PrepData.(database).(subjectNo).(segmentNo).signal;
imfSum = 0;
sigSum = 0;
% Performing EMD
[imf, ~] = emd(currentSig, 'Display', 0);
% Calculating the noise level
Vn = alpha*max(currentSig);
% Calculating the noise level crossing ratio
for k = 1:length(imf(:,1))
if abs(imf(k,1))<=Vn
imfSum = imfSum + (imf(k,1)^2);
sigSum = sigSum + (currentSig(k)^2);
end
end
NLCR = imfSum/sigSum;
% Defining the first IMF and residue based on the NLCR
133
==PAGE:159==
C.2. FUNCTIONS
Reference Algorithm
Implementation
if NLCR <= beta
IMF1 = imf(:,1)+imf(:,2);
R = currentSig −IMF1;
else
IMF1 = imf(:,1);
R = currentSig −IMF1 −imf(:,2);
end
% Saving additional data in the struct
if testCondition == 0
EMDData.(databases{db}).(subjectNo).(segmentNo).label = ...
PrepData.(database).(subjectNo).(segmentNo).label;
EMDData.(databases{db}).(subjectNo).(segmentNo).featureLabels = ...
PrepData.(database).(subjectNo).(segmentNo).featureLabels;
end
EMDData.(databases{db}).(subjectNo).(segmentNo).subjectID = ...
PrepData.(database).(subjectNo).(segmentNo).subjectID;
% Calculating FFTs
signalFFT = fftshift(fft(currentSig));
IMF1FFT = fftshift(fft(IMF1));
RFFT = fftshift(fft(R));
% Calculating cosine similarity measures
EMDData.(databases{db}).(subjectNo).(segmentNo).simIMF = ...
cosine_similarity(signalFFT,IMF1FFT);
EMDData.(databases{db}).(subjectNo).(segmentNo).simR = ...
cosine_similarity(signalFFT,RFFT);
end
end
end
C.2.3.1
Cosine Similarity
function [similarity] = cosine_similarity(sig1, sig2)
%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%
%
% DESCRIPTION: This function calculates the cosine similarity measure of
%
two signals.
%
% INPUT:
%
o sig1: The first signal
%
o sig2: The second signal
%
% OUTPUT:
%
o similarity: The cosine similarity measure
%
% AUTHORS: Maria L. Sakhat (s154553) & Lena M. Nilsson (s153554)
%
%
% DATE CREATED: 01−10−20
% DATE MODIFIED: 01−10−20
134
==PAGE:160==
C.2. FUNCTIONS
Reference Algorithm
Implementation
%
%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%
% Calculating the normalization factor
normalization = norm(sig1,2)*norm(sig2,2);
% Preallocation
similarity = zeros(length(sig1),1);
% Calculating the cosine similarity measure
for i = 1:length(sig1)
similarity(i) = (abs(sig1(i))*abs(sig2(i)))/normalization;
end
end

function [finalPerformance] = selection_classification(EMDData, databases)
%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%
%
% DESCRIPTION: This function performs feature selection using a random
%
forest algorithm and classification with an SVM classifier.
%
% INPUT:
%
o EMDData: Struct containing each data segment for each subject for each
%
database after preprocessing
%
.(databases): ID of the database
%
.(subjectNo): ID of the subject
%
.(segmentNo): ID of the segment
%
.label: The label for the segment
%
.subjectID: The subject ID for the segment
%
.featureLabels: A vector including label conditions
%
.simIMF: Similarity measure of DFT of the signal and
%
DFT of IMF
%
.simR: Similarity measure of DFT of the signal and
%
DFT of residue
%
o databases: The wanted database name(s)
%
% OUTPUT:
%
o finalPerformance: Struct containing mean and std performance measures
%
.mean.Se: Mean sensitivity
%
.mean.Sp: Mean specificity
%
.mean.Ac: Mean accuracy
%
.mean.Gmean: Mean G−mean accuracy
%
.std.Se: Mean sensitivity standard deviation
%
.std.Sp: Mean specificity standard deviation
%
.std.Ac: Mean accuracy standard deviation
%
.std.Gmean: Mean G−mean accuracy standard deviation
%
% AUTHORS: Maria L. Sakhat (s154553) & Lena M. Nilsson (s153554)
%
%
135
==PAGE:161==
C.2. FUNCTIONS
Reference Algorithm
Implementation
% DATE CREATED: 01−10−20
% DATE MODIFIED: 14−10−20
%
%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%
%% CREATE FEATURE STRUCTS
% Initialize
countVF = 0;
countNonVF = 0;
for db = 1:numel(fieldnames(EMDData))
database = databases{db};
for i = 1:numel(fieldnames(EMDData.(database)))
subjectNo = sprintf('subject%d',i);
for j = 1:numel(fieldnames(EMDData.(database).(subjectNo)))
segmentNo = sprintf('seg%d',j);
% Divide into VF and non−VF
% VF if 100% of samples are VF
if EMDData.(database).(subjectNo).(segmentNo).featureLabels(10) == 1
countVF = countVF + 1;
VFFeatures(countVF,:) = ...
[EMDData.(database).(subjectNo).(segmentNo).simIMF; ...
EMDData.(database).(subjectNo).(segmentNo).simR];
% Non−VF if less than 100% of samples are VF
else
countNonVF = countNonVF + 1;
nonVFFeatures(countNonVF,:) = ...
[EMDData.(database).(subjectNo).(segmentNo).simIMF; ...
EMDData.(database).(subjectNo).(segmentNo).simR];
end
end
end
end
% Creating label vector and concatenating features
VFLabels = ones(size(VFFeatures,1),1);
nonVFLabels = zeros(size(nonVFFeatures,1),1);
labels = [VFLabels; nonVFLabels];
features = [VFFeatures; nonVFFeatures];
%% FEATURE SELECTION (RANDOM FOREST)
% Training random forest classifier model
Mdl = fitcensemble(features, labels,...
'NumLearningCycles',750,...
'Method','Bag',...
'OptimizeHyperparameters','none',...
'HyperparameterOptimizationOptions',struct('UseParallel',true));
% Ranking the features after importance
Im = predictorImportance(Mdl);
%% UPSAMPLING (SMOTE)
% Picking the top 24% most important features
136
==PAGE:162==
C.2. FUNCTIONS
Reference Algorithm
Implementation
[~, loc] = sort(Im,'descend');
topFeatures = loc(1:(0.24*length(Im)));
% Limiting to the chosen features
chosenVFFeatures = VFFeatures(:,topFeatures);
chosenNonVFFeatures = nonVFFeatures(:,topFeatures);
% Upsampling VF using SMOTE
[X,~,~,~] = smote(chosenVFFeatures, 5, 5);
% Collecting the non−VF and VF features
chosenFeat = [X; chosenNonVFFeatures];
% Upsampling using SMOTE
chosenLab = [ones(size(X,1),1); zeros(size(nonVFFeatures,1),1)];
[finalFeatures,label,~,~] = smote(chosenFeat, [], 5, 'Class',chosenLab);
%% CLASSIFICATION (SVM)
% Shuffling the feature order
r = randperm(size(finalFeatures,1));
set = finalFeatures(r,:);
labels = label(r,:);
% Creating cross−validation partition
cvpart = cvpartition(length(set),'kfold',10);
% Performing 10−fold cross−validation
for k = 1:10
% Getting training and test indices
trainingData = training(cvpart,k);
testData = test(cvpart,k);
% Training SVM model
SVMModel = fitcsvm(set(trainingData,:),labels(trainingData),...
'KernelFunction','RBF',...
'BoxConstraint',100,'KernelScale',sqrt(1/45), ...
'OptimizeHyperparameters','none',...
'HyperparameterOptimizationOptions',struct('UseParallel',true));
% Classifying using the trained SVM model
ypred = predict(SVMModel,set(testData,:));
% Calculating performance measures
Performance = classification_performance(ypred, labels(testData));
% Saving performance measures for each fold
sensitivityK(k) = Performance.se;
specificityK(k) = Performance.sp;
accuracyK(k) = Performance.ac;
gMeanK(k) = Performance.gMeanAcc;
end
% The mean of each performance measure
finalPerformance.mean.Se = mean(sensitivityK);
finalPerformance.mean.Sp = mean(specificityK);

finalPerformance.std.Se = std(sensitivityK);
finalPerformance.std.Sp = std(specificityK);
finalPerformance.std.Ac = std(accuracyK);
finalPerformance.std.Gmean = std(gMeanK);

C.2.4.1
SMOTE
This code is written by Bjarke Skogstad Larsen. [37]
% SMOTE: Synthetic Minority Over−sampling Technique
% This function is based on the paper referenced below −with a few
% additional optional functionalities.
% DOI: https://doi.org/10.1613/jair.953
%
% This function synthesizes new observations based on existing (input)
% data, and a k−nearest neighbor approach. If multiple classes are given as
% input, only neighbors within the same class are considered.
% This function can be used to over−sample minority classes in a dataset.
%
%
Use:
%
[X,C,Xn,Cn] = smote(X, [N, k], {options})
%
%
Input:
%
X: Original dataset. Each row is an observation, and each column a
%
different feature.
%
N: Amount of oversampling (Default: 1 = 100% doubles the observations)
%
If 'Class' is set, then N can be a vector with number of
%
elements equal to the number of classes. Elements of N should be
%
sorted according to the sorted unique classes.
%
If N is empty, then 'balancing' will occur, synthesizing
%
minority classes to the same number as the majority class.
%
k: Number of nearest neighbors to consider (Default: 5)
%
If 'Class' is set, then k can be a vector with number of
%
elements equal to the number of classes. Elements of k should be
%
sorted according to the sorted unique classes.
%
Note that number of nearest neighbors to consider must be equal
%
to or greater than the number of times an observation is used
%
for synthesizing a new observation: N or SynthObs (if set).
%
Options:
%
SynthObs: Overrides N, and sets the amount of synthesization for
%
each observation directly. If SynthObs is set, no
%
balancing will occur, regardless of N being empty.
%
Class:
Sets the class for each observation. Nearest neighbors
%
are only found within the same class.
%
%
Output:
%
X: Complete dataset (original and synthesized)
138
==PAGE:164==
C.2. FUNCTIONS
Reference Algorithm
Implementation
%
C: Classes of complete dataset
%
Xn: Synthesized observations
%
Cn: Classes of synthesized observations
%
%
Examples:
%
X = smote(X, 1.5, 4)
%
Synthesizes 150% new observations using a randomly picked of the 4
%
nearest neighbors and the observation itself. In this case each
%
observation is used as basis 1−2 times. Which is used 1 and which 2
%
times are chosen at random.
%
%
[X,C] = smote(X, [], 'Class', C)
%
Synthesizes new observations of minority classes, so number of
%
observations for each class matches the number of observations of
%
the majority class. Using the default 5 nearest neighbors in this
%
example.
%
% Author: Bjarke Skogstad Larsen <bjarke.skogstad@acarix.com>
% Updated: 2020−05−07
function [X,C,Xn,Cn] = smote(X, N, k, options)
arguments
X (:,:) % Observation Matrix
N (:,1) double {mustBeNonnegative} = 1 % Amount of synthesization
k (:,1) double {mustBePositive,mustBeInteger} = 5 % Number of nearest
% neighbors to consider
options.Class (:,1) {mustBeSameSize(options.Class,X)} % Class vector:
% Determines the class of each observation
options.SynthObs (:,1) {mustBeSameSize(options.SynthObs,X)} % Synthesization
% vector. Determines how many times each observation is used as a
% base for synthesization
end
% Handle optional Class vector
if isfield(options,'Class')
C = options.Class;
else
C = ones(size(X,1),1); % If no Class vector is given, default all
% observations to the same class: [1]
end
uC = unique(C); % Class list
nC = groupcounts(C); % Number of observations of each class
% Handle N −must have one number for each class
if isempty(N) % Do balancing if N is empty
if numel(uC)<2 % Class vector must contain at least two classes to balance
error('Class vector must contain at least 2 classes to balance.');
end
N = max(nC)./nC−1; % Calculate over−sampling percentage for each
% class to attain equal number of observations as majority class
elseif isscalar(N)
N = repmat(N,numel(uC),1);
elseif ~isvector(N) || numel(N)~=numel(uC)
error('N must either be empty, a scalar, or a vector with same
139
==PAGE:165==
C.2. FUNCTIONS
Reference Algorithm
Implementation
number of elements as unique classes.');
end
% Handle k −must have one number for each class
if isscalar(k)
k = repmat(k,numel(uC),1);
elseif ~isvector(k) || numel(k)~=numel(uC)
error('k must either be a scalar or a vector with same number of
elements as unique classes.');
end
% Decide on how many of each observation (in case of non−integer,
% 'extras' will be chosen at random). Vector J determines how many of
% each observation is used as a base for synthesization.
if isfield(options,'SynthObs')
J = options.SynthObs;
else
J = nan(size(X,1),1); % Synthesization vector
for ii=1:numel(uC) % Iterate through the classes
iC = find(C==uC(ii));
P = randperm(nC(ii),round(rem(N(ii),1)*nC(ii))); % Randomly pick
% indexes of 'extras'
J(iC) = ones(nC(ii),1)*floor(N(ii)); % First distribute evenly
J(iC(P)) = J(iC(P))+1; % Then assign the 'extras'
end
end
% Synthesize observations
Xn = []; % TODO: Consider pre−allocating memory
Cn = []; % TODO: Consider pre−allocating memory
for ii=1:numel(uC)
iC = C==uC(ii);
if sum(J(iC))>0 % Skip synthesization attempt if no observations are
% synthesized for this class (for speed)
Xnn = simpleSMOTE(X(iC,:),J(iC),k(ii));
Xn = [Xn;Xnn]; % TODO: Consider pre−allocating memory
Cn = [Cn;repmat(uC(ii),size(Xnn,1),1)]; % TODO: Consider pre−allocating memory
end
end
% Set output
X = [X;Xn];
C = [C;Cn];
end
% This is where the magic happens ;−)
%
X : Observational matrix (rows are observations, columns are variables)
%
J : Synthesization vector. It has the same length as the number of
%
observations (rows) in X. J determines how many times each
%
observation is used as a base for synthesization.
%
k : Number of nearest neighbors to consider when synthesizing.
function Xn = simpleSMOTE(X,J,k)
[idx, ~] = knnsearch(X,X,'k',k+1); % Find nearest neighbors (add one to
% the number of neighbors to find, as observations are their own nearest neighbor)
Xn = nan(sum(J),size(X,2)); % Pre−allocate memory for synthesized observations
140
==PAGE:166==
C.2. FUNCTIONS
Reference Algorithm
Implementation
% Iterate through observations to create to synthesize new observations
for ii=1:numel(J)
P = randperm(k,J(ii))+1; % Randomize nearest neighbor pick (never pick
% first nearest neighbor as this is the observation itself)
for jj=1:J(ii)
x = X(idx(ii,1),:); % Observation
xk = X(idx(ii,P(jj)),:); % Nearest neighbor
Xn(sum(J(1:ii−1))+jj,:) = (xk−x)*rand+x; % Synthesize observation
end
end
end
% Argument validation
function mustBeSameSize(a,b)
if ~isequal(size(a,1),size(b,1))
error('Must have the same number of elements as number of observations
(rows) in X.');
end
end

function [Performance] = classification_performance(predictions, labels)
%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%
%
% DESCRIPTION: This function calculates the sensitivity, specificity,
%
accuracy and G−mean accuracy of the input predictions and labels.
%
% INPUT:
%
o predictions: Vector containing binary predictions
%
o labels: Vector containing binary labels
%
% OUTPUT:
%
o Performance: Struct containing performance measures
%
.se: Sensitivity
%
.sp: Specificity
%
.ac: Accuracy
%
.gMeanAcc: G−mean accuracy
%
% AUTHORS: Maria L. Sakhat (s154553) & Lena M. Nilsson (s153554)
%
%
% DATE CREATED: 05−10−20
% DATE MODIFIED: 05−10−20
%
%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%
% Preallocation
TP = 0; TN = 0; FP = 0; FN = 0;
for i = 1:length(predictions)
141
==PAGE:167==
C.2. FUNCTIONS
Reference Algorithm
Implementation
% If the prediction and label are the same
if isequal(predictions(i), labels(i))
switch predictions(i)
case 1
TP = TP + 1; % True positive
case 0
TN = TN + 1; % True negative
end
% If the prediction and label are different
else
switch predictions(i)
case 0
FN = FN + 1; % False negative
case 1
FP = FP + 1; % False positive
end
end
end
% Compressing variables into struct
Performance.se = TP/(TP+FN);
Performance.sp = TN/(TN+FP);
Performance.ac = (TP+TN)/(TP+FP+TN+FN);
Performance.gMeanAcc = sqrt(Performance.se*Performance.sp);
end

function [Data,fs] = data_segmentation(databases)
%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%
%
% DESCRIPTION: This function loads data and divides it into 5 second
%
segments, adding a label to each segment.
%
% INPUT:
%
o databases: The wanted database name(s)
%
% OUTPUT:
%
o Data: Struct containing each data segment for each subject for each
%
database
%
.(databases): ID of the database
%
.(subjectNo): ID of the subject
%
.(segmentNo): ID of the segment
%
.label: The label for the segment
%
.signal: The signal for the segment
%
.subjectID: The subject ID for the segment
%
.featureLabels: A vector including label conditions
%
o fs: Sampling frequency
%
% AUTHORS: Maria L. Sakhat (s154553) & Lena M. Nilsson (s153554)
%
%
% DATE CREATED: 14−10−20
% DATE MODIFIED: 09−11−20
%
%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%
%% DATA SEGMENTATION
for db = 1:length(databases)
%% LOAD DATA
DataStruct = loading_data(databases{db});
%% UNWRAP VARIABLES
tm = DataStruct.tm;
signal = DataStruct.signal;
ann = DataStruct.ann;
beatType = DataStruct.beatType;
annType = DataStruct.annType;
fs = DataStruct.fs;
144
==PAGE:170==
D.2. FUNCTIONS
VT/VF Algorithm Implementation
numberOfSubjects = DataStruct.numberOfSubjects;
%% CREATE LABEL VECTOR
% Determine the label types available for the current database
if strcmp(databases{db},'cudb')
labelTypes = {'(N';'(VT';'(VF'};
elseif strcmp(databases{db},'vfdb')
labelTypes = {'(N';'(NSR';'(NOISE';'(VT';'(VFIB';'(VF'; '(VFL'};
end
% Preallocations
labelVec = ones(numberOfSubjects,length(signal{1}));
labelVec2 = ones(numberOfSubjects,length(signal{1}));
startIdx = [];
endIdx = [];
% Create a label vector for each subject
for i = 1:numberOfSubjects
switch databases{db}
case 'vfdb'
% Determine the type of annotation
annotation = annType{i};
annLocation = ann{i};
% If only one annotation is present
if length(annotation) == 1
% Determine the type of annotation
[~, label] = ismember(annotation,labelTypes);
% Insert the label in the label vector
labelVec(i,annLocation:end) = label;
% If more than one annotation is present
elseif length(annotation) > 1
% Loop through the annotations
for j = 1:length(annotation)
% Add the end index to the annotation locations
annLocation1 = [annLocation; length(labelVec)];
% Determine the type of annotation
[~, label] = ismember(annotation(j),labelTypes);
% Insert the label in the label vector
labelVec(i,annLocation1(j):annLocation1(j+1)) = label;
end
end
case 'cudb'
% Rhythm annotations
% Locate all the non−empty cells
annLoc = find(cellfun(@isempty,annType{i})==0);
% Determine the type of annotation
annotation = annType{i}(annLoc);
annLocation = ann{i}(annLoc);
% If only one annotation is present
if length(annotation) == 1
% Determine the type of annotation
[~, label] = ismember(annotation,labelTypes);
% Insert the label in the label vector
labelVec(i,annLocation:end) = label;
145
==PAGE:171==
D.2. FUNCTIONS
VT/VF Algorithm Implementation
% If more than one annotation is present
elseif length(annotation) > 1
% Loop through the annotations
for j = 1:length(annotation)
% Add the end index to the annotation locations
annLocation1 = [annLocation; length(labelVec)];
% Determine the type of annotation
[~, label] = ismember(annotation(j),labelTypes);
% Insert the label in the label vector
labelVec(i,annLocation1(j):annLocation1(j+1)) = label;
end
end
% Beat annotations
% Iterating through the beat annotations
for n = 1:length(beatType{i})−1
% Defining location vector for indicing
if n == 1
location = [1; ann{i}(n)];
else
location = ann{i}(n);
location = [location; ann{i}(n+1)];
end
% Determine the type of annotation
if beatType{i}(n) == 'N'
% Insert the label in the label vector
labelVec2(i,location(1):location(2)) = 1;
elseif beatType{i}(n) == '['
% Create start index for label vector
startIdx = [startIdx; location(1)];
elseif beatType{i}(n) == ']'
% Create end index for label vector
endIdx = [endIdx; location(1)];
else
% Set to non−VT/VF
labelVec2(i,location(1):location(2)) = 1;
end
end
% If the segment ends in VT/VF
if length(startIdx)>length(endIdx)
% Insert the label in the label vector
labelVec2(i,startIdx:end) = 3;
% Otherwise
else
% Insert the label in the label vector
labelVec2(i,startIdx:endIdx) = 3;
end
% Clear the indices
startIdx = [];
endIdx = [];
% Beat annotations of cudb override rhythm annotations
labelVec(labelVec2==3) = 3;
end
end

==PAGE:172==
D.2. FUNCTIONS
VT/VF Algorithm Implementation
% Extract only the wanted annotations
if strcmp(databases{db},'vfdb')
labelVec(labelVec == 2) = 1; % SR is set to non−VT/VF
labelVec(labelVec == 5) = 4; % VFIB is set to VT/VF
labelVec(labelVec == 6) = 4; % VF is set to VT/VF
labelVec(labelVec == 7) = 4; % VFL is set to VT/VF
labelVec(labelVec == 3) = 1; % Noise is set to non−VT/VF
labelVec(labelVec == 0) = 1; % Everything else is set to non−VT/VF
elseif strcmp(databases{db},'cudb')
labelVec(labelVec == 3) = 4; % VF is set to VT/VF
labelVec(labelVec == 2) = 4; % VT is set to VT/VF
labelVec(labelVec == 0) = 1; % Everything else is set to non−VT/VF
end
%% CREATE SEGMENTS
segmentLength = 5; % Seconds
windowSize = segmentLength*fs;
windowShift =
1*fs;
% Initialize variables
nonVTVF = 0;
VTVF = 0;
enhancedAnnotationVec = 0.1:0.1:1;
for i = 1:numberOfSubjects
count = 1;
startIdx = 1;
endIdx = windowSize;
subjectNo = sprintf('subject%d',i);
% Loop through all possible segments in the signal
while endIdx<length(labelVec)
segmentNo = sprintf('seg%d',count);
% Exclude noise and NaNs
if sum(isnan(signal{i}(startIdx:endIdx,1)))==0
Data.(databases{db}).(subjectNo).(segmentNo).subjectID = i;
Data.(databases{db}).(subjectNo).(segmentNo).signal = ...
signal{i}(startIdx:endIdx,1);
sumNonVTVF = sum(labelVec(i,startIdx:endIdx)==1);
sumVTVF = sum(labelVec(i,startIdx:endIdx)==4);
% If VT/VF samples are present
if sumVTVF ~= 0
% Determine the percentage of VT/VF samples in the segment
Data.(databases{db}).(subjectNo).(segmentNo).featureLabels = ...
repelem(sumVTVF/(sumNonVTVF+sumVTVF),10)>=enhancedAnnotationVec;
% If no VT/VF samples are present
else
% All percentages are set to 0
Data.(databases{db}).(subjectNo).(segmentNo).featureLabels =...
false(1,10);
end
147
==PAGE:173==
D.2. FUNCTIONS
VT/VF Algorithm Implementation
% If the majority of samples are non−VT/VF, the label is non−VT/VF
if
sumNonVTVF > sumVTVF
Data.(databases{db}).(subjectNo).(segmentNo).label = 'nonVTVF';
nonVTVF = nonVTVF + 1;
% If the majority of samples are VT/VF, the label is VT/VF
elseif sumVTVF >= sumNonVTVF
Data.(databases{db}).(subjectNo).(segmentNo).label = 'VTVF';
VTVF = VTVF + 1;
end
count = count+1;
end
% Move the window
startIdx = startIdx + windowShift;
endIdx = startIdx + windowSize−1;
end
end
end
end

function [topFeatures, SVMModel, Performance, scoreSVMModel, newPerformance] = ...
selection_classification(EMDData, databases)
%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%
%
% DESCRIPTION: This function performs feature selection using a ReliefF
%
algorithm and classification with an SVM classifier.
%
% INPUT:
%
o EMDData: Struct containing each data segment for each subject for each
%
database after preprocessing
%
.(databases): ID of the database
%
.(subjectNo): ID of the subject
%
.(segmentNo): ID of the segment
152
==PAGE:178==
D.2. FUNCTIONS
VT/VF Algorithm Implementation
%
.label: The label for the segment
%
.subjectID: The subject ID for the segment
%
.featureLabels: A vector including label conditions
%
.simIMF: Similarity measure of DFT of the signal and
%
DFT of IMF
%
.simR: Similarity measure of DFT of the signal and
%
DFT of residue
%
o databases: The wanted database name(s)
%
% OUTPUT:
%
o topFeatures: Features selected from the ReliefF algorithm
%
o SVMModel: Trained SVM classifier model
%
o Performance: Struct containing performance measures
%
.se: Sensitivity
%
.sp: Specificity
%
.ac: Accuracy
%
.pp: Positive predictive value
%
o scoreSVMModel: Trained SVM classifier model including the transformation
%
function for the optimal score−to−posterior−probability
%
o newPerformance: Struct containing performance measures based on new
%
predictions made with a classification threshold
%
.se: Sensitivity
%
.sp: Specificity
%
.ac: Accuracy
%
.pp: Positive predictive value
%
% AUTHORS: Maria L. Sakhat (s154553) & Lena M. Nilsson (s153554)
%
%
% DATE CREATED: 14−10−20
% DATE MODIFIED: 02−01−21
%
%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%
%% CREATE FEATURE STRUCTS
% Initialize
countVTVF = 0;
countNonVTVF = 0;
% Preallocation for Fs = 250 Hz
VTVFFeatures = zeros(9638,2500);
nonVTVFFeatures = zeros(52927,2500);
% Preallocation for Fs = 100 Hz
% VTVFFeatures = zeros(9638,1000);
% nonVTVFFeatures = zeros(52927,1000);
for db = 1:numel(fieldnames(EMDData))
database = databases{db};
for i = 1:numel(fieldnames(EMDData.(database)))
subjectNo = sprintf('subject%d',i);
for j = 1:numel(fieldnames(EMDData.(database).(subjectNo)))
segmentNo = sprintf('seg%d',j);
% Divide into VT/VF and non−VT/VF
% VT/VF if 100% of the samples are VT/VF
153
==PAGE:179==
D.2. FUNCTIONS
VT/VF Algorithm Implementation
if EMDData.(database).(subjectNo).(segmentNo).featureLabels(10) == 1
countVTVF = countVTVF + 1;
VTVFFeatures(countVTVF,:) = ...
[EMDData.(database).(subjectNo).(segmentNo).simIMF; ...
EMDData.(database).(subjectNo).(segmentNo).simR];
% Non−VT/VF if less than 100% of the samples are VT/VF
else
countNonVTVF = countNonVTVF + 1;
nonVTVFFeatures(countNonVTVF,:) = ...
[EMDData.(database).(subjectNo).(segmentNo).simIMF; ...
EMDData.(database).(subjectNo).(segmentNo).simR];
end
end
end
end
% Creating label vectors
VTVFLabels = ones(size(VTVFFeatures,1),1);
nonVTVFLabels = zeros(size(nonVTVFFeatures,1),1);
% Creating train set with 80% of the data
VTVFTrain = VTVFFeatures(1:floor(0.8*size(VTVFFeatures,1)),:);
nonVTVFTrain = nonVTVFFeatures(1:floor(0.8*size(nonVTVFFeatures,1)),:);
VTVFTrainLab = VTVFLabels(1:floor(0.8*size(VTVFLabels,1)),:);
nonVTVFTrainLab = nonVTVFLabels(1:floor(0.8*size(nonVTVFLabels,1)),:);
trainingFeatures = [VTVFTrain; nonVTVFTrain];
trainingLabels = [VTVFTrainLab; nonVTVFTrainLab];
% Creating test set with 20% of the data
VTVFTest = VTVFFeatures(floor(0.8*size(VTVFFeatures,1))+1:end,:);
nonVTVFTest = nonVTVFFeatures(floor(0.8*size(nonVTVFFeatures,1))+1:end,:);
%% FEATURE SELECTION (RELIEFF)
% Ranking importance of features using ReliefF algorithm
[~, weights] = relieff(trainingFeatures, trainingLabels, 5, 'method', ...
'classification');
% Picking the top 41% most important features
[~, loc] = sort(weights, 'descend');
topFeatures = loc(1:floor((0.41*length(weights))));
%% UPSAMPLING TRAIN (SMOTE)
% Limiting to the chosen features
chosenVTVFFeatures = VTVFTrain(:,topFeatures);
chosenNonVTVFFeatures = nonVTVFTrain(:,topFeatures);
% Upsampling VT/VF using SMOTE
[X,~,~,~] = smote(chosenVTVFFeatures, 3, 5);
% Collecting non−VT/VF and VT/VF features
chosenFeat = [X; chosenNonVTVFFeatures];
154
==PAGE:180==
D.2. FUNCTIONS
VT/VF Algorithm Implementation
% Upsampling using SMOTE
chosenLab = [ones(size(X,1),1); zeros(size(chosenNonVTVFFeatures,1),1)];
[finalTrainFeat,finalTrainLab,~,~] = smote(chosenFeat, [], 5, 'Class',chosenLab);
%% UPSAMPLING TEST (SMOTE)
% Limiting to the chosen features
chosenVTVFFeatures = VTVFTest(:,topFeatures);
chosenNonVTVFFeatures = nonVTVFTest(:,topFeatures);
% Upsampling VT/VF using SMOTE
[X,~,~,~] = smote(chosenVTVFFeatures, 3, 5);
% Collecting non−VT/VF and VT/VF features
chosenFeat = [X; chosenNonVTVFFeatures];
% Upsampling using SMOTE
chosenLab = [ones(size(X,1),1); zeros(size(chosenNonVTVFFeatures,1),1)];
[finalTestFeat,finalTestLab,~,~] = smote(chosenFeat, [], 5, 'Class',chosenLab);
%% CLASSIFICATION (SVM)
% Training SVM model
SVMModel = fitcsvm(finalTrainFeat,finalTrainLab,...
'KernelFunction','RBF',...
'BoxConstraint',30,'KernelScale',0.68,...
'OptimizeHyperparameters','none',...
'HyperparameterOptimizationOptions',struct('UseParallel',true));
% Classifying using the trained SVM model
ypred = predict(SVMModel,finalTestFeat);
% Calculating performance measures
Performance = classification_performance(ypred, finalTestLab);
% Fitting a posterior probability
[scoreSVMModel, scoreTransform] = fitPosterior(SVMModel);
[~, prob] = predict(scoreSVMModel, finalTestFeat);
% Classification thresholds
vec = 0.01:0.01:0.99;
% Iterating through different classification thresholds
for k = 1:length(vec)
% Iterating through observations
for i = 1:length(prob)
if prob(i,1) > vec(k)
% If the posterior probability of belonging to the non−VT/VF class is
% larger than the classification threshold, the prediction is 0
ypredNew(i,1) = 0;
elseif prob(i,2) > vec(end+1−k)
% If the posterior probability of belonging to the VT/VF class is
% larger than the classification threshold, the prediction is 1
155
==PAGE:181==
D.2. FUNCTIONS
VT/VF Algorithm Implementation
ypredNew(i,1) = 1;
end
end
% Calculating performance measures based on the new predictions
newPerformance = classification_performance(ypredNew, finalTestLab);
end
end
D.2.2.1
Classiﬁcation Performance
function [Performance] = classification_performance(predictions, labels)
%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%
%
% DESCRIPTION: This function calculates the sensitivity, specificity,
%
accuracy and G−mean accuracy of the input predictions and labels.
%
% INPUT:
%
o predictions: Vector containing binary predictions
%
o labels: Vector containing binary labels
%
% OUTPUT:
%
o Performance: Struct containing performance measures
%
.se: Sensitivity
%
.sp: Specificity
%
.ac: Accuracy
%
.pp: Positive predictive value
%
% AUTHORS: Maria L. Sakhat (s154553) & Lena M. Nilsson (s153554)
%
%
% DATE CREATED: 14−10−20
% DATE MODIFIED: 14−10−20
%
%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%
% Preallocation
TP = 0; TN = 0; FP = 0; FN = 0;
for i = 1:length(predictions)
% If the prediction and label are the same
if isequal(predictions(i), labels(i))
switch predictions(i)
case 1
TP = TP + 1; % True positive
case 0
TN = TN + 1; % True negative
end
% If the prediction and label are different
else
switch predictions(i)
case 0
156
==PAGE:182==
D.3. VERIFICATION
VT/VF Algorithm Implementation
FN = FN + 1; % False negative
case 1
FP = FP + 1; % False positive
end
end
end
% Compressing variables into struct
Performance.se = TP/(TP+FN);
Performance.sp = TN/(TN+FP);
Performance.ac = (TP+TN)/(TP+FP+TN+FN);
Performance.pp = TP/(TP+FP);
end

endIdx = startIdx + windowSize−1;

function [predictions] = classification_db(scoreSVMModel, topFeatures,...
EMDData, databases)
%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

DFT of residue

% OUTPUT:

% AUTHORS: Maria L. Sakhat (s154553) & Lena M. Nilsson (s153554)

% DATE MODIFIED: 23−11−20

newFeatures = [];

database = databases{db};
for i = 1:numel(fieldnames(EMDData.(database)))
subjectNo = sprintf('subject%d',i);

segmentNo = sprintf('seg%d',j);

end

clear EMDData
% Classifying using the trained SVM model
[~, predictions] = predict(scoreSVMModel,features(:,topFeatures));
end

annLocation(ismember(annLocation, locOne+1:locTwo−1)) = [];
else
% Count each time no samples are removed

count = count + 1;

[~, locEnd] = min(abs(timeWARDAligned(end) −th));

annLocationAligned2 = annLocationAligned(annLocationAligned <= locEnd);
annotationsAligned2 = annotationsAligned(annLocationAligned <= locEnd);

annLocationAligned3 = annLocationAligned2 −(locStart−1);

E.3. FUNCTIONS
VT/VF Algorithm Implementation
for WARD System
% Determine the type of annotation
[~, label] = ismember(annotations(l),labelTypes);
% If the label is VT/VF start the annotation between the current
% and previous annotation
if label == 2
% Insert the label in the label vector
labelVec(annLocation1(l)−floor(length(annLocation1(l−1):...
annLocation1(l))/2):annLocation1(l+1)) = label;
else
% Insert the label in the label vector
labelVec(annLocation1(l):annLocation1(l+1)) = label;
end
end
% Set everything except VT/VF to non−VT/VF

% Initializing variables
VTVF = 0;
nonVTVF = 0;
enhancedAnnotationVec = 0.1:0.1:1;

windowShift =
1*fs;
% Initializations
signal = ecgData;
count = 1;
startIdx = 1;
endIdx = windowSize;
subjectNo = sprintf('subject%d',i);
% Loop through all possible segments in the signal
while endIdx<length(labelVec)
segmentNo = sprintf('seg%d',count);
% Exclude noise and NaNs
if sum(isnan(signal(startIdx:endIdx,1)))==0
Data.(database).(subjectNo).(segmentNo).subjectID = i;
Data.(database).(subjectNo).(segmentNo).signal = ...
signal(startIdx:endIdx,1);
% Extract the number of VT/VF and non−VT/VF samples in the segment
sumNonVTVF = sum(labelVec(startIdx:endIdx)==1);
sumVTVF = sum(labelVec(startIdx:endIdx)==2);
% If VT/VF samples are present
if sumVTVF ~= 0
% Determine the percentage of VT/VF samples in the segment
Data.(database).(subjectNo).(segmentNo).featureLabels = ...
repelem(sumVTVF/(sumNonVTVF+sumVTVF),10)>=enhancedAnnotationVec;
% If no VT/VF samples are present
168
==PAGE:194==
E.3. FUNCTIONS
VT/VF Algorithm Implementation
for WARD System
else
% All percentages are set to 0
Data.(database).(subjectNo).(segmentNo).featureLabels =...
false(1,10);
end
% If the majority of samples are non−VT/VF, the label is non−VT/VF
if sumVTVF < sumNonVTVF
Data.(database).(subjectNo).(segmentNo).label = 'nonVTVF';
nonVTVF = nonVTVF + 1;
% If the majority of samples are VT/VF, the label is VT/VF
elseif sumVTVF >= sumNonVTVF
Data.(database).(subjectNo).(segmentNo).label = 'VTVF';
VTVF = VTVF + 1;
end
count = count+1;
end
% Move the window
startIdx = startIdx + windowShift;
endIdx = startIdx + windowSize−1;
end
end

function [EMDData] = feature_extraction_rar(PrepData, databases)
%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%
%
% DESCRIPTION: This function computes the EMD and DFT of each segment of
%
data, and then extracts features using cosine similarity
%
measure. Additional features are also computed.
%
% INPUT:
%
o PrepData: Struct containing each data segment for each subject for each
%
database after preprocessing
%
.(databases): ID of the database
%
.(subjectNo): ID of the subject
%
.(segmentNo): ID of the segment
%
.label: The label for the segment
%
.signal: The signal for the segment
%
.subjectID: The subject ID for the segment
%
.featureLabels: A vector including label conditions
%
o databases: The wanted database name(s)
%
% OUTPUT:
%
o EMDData: Struct containing each data segment for each subject for each
%
database after preprocessing
%
.(databases): ID of the database
%
.(subjectNo): ID of the subject
%
.(segmentNo): ID of the segment
169
==PAGE:195==
E.3. FUNCTIONS
VT/VF Algorithm Implementation
for WARD System
%
.label: The label for the segment
%
.subjectID: The subject ID for the segment
%
.featureLabels: A vector including label conditions
%
.simIMF: Similarity measure of a DFT of the signal and
%
a DFT of IMF
%
.simR: Similarity measure of a DFT of the signal and
%
a DFT of residue
%
.envDiffMean: Mean of a differentiated vector
%
consisting of five mean envelope
%
values of each second
%
.envDiffMax: Maximum of a differentiated vector
%
consisting of five mean envelope
%
values of each second
%
.envSum: Sum of the upper envelope
%
.accMean: Mean of an acceleration vector
%
.accMax: Maximum of an acceleration vector
%
.accDiff: Difference between the maximum and minimum
%
of an acceleration vector
%
.outlierFeat: Number of outliers in a segment
%
% AUTHORS: Maria L. Sakhat (s154553) & Lena M. Nilsson (s153554)
%
%
% DATE CREATED: 22−12−20
% DATE MODIFIED: 10−01−21
%
%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%
%% FEATURE EXTRACTION
% Defining parameters
alpha = 0.05;
beta = 0.02;
% Performing EMD for every segment
for db = 1:numel(fieldnames(PrepData))
database = databases{db};
for i = 1:numel(fieldnames(PrepData.(database)))
subjectNo = sprintf('subject%d',i);
for j = 1:numel(fieldnames(PrepData.(database).(subjectNo)))
segmentNo = sprintf('seg%d',j);
currentSig = PrepData.(database).(subjectNo).(segmentNo).signal;
imfSum = 0;
sigSum = 0;
% Performing EMD
[imf, ~] = emd(currentSig, 'Display', 0);
% Calculating the noise level
Vn = alpha*max(currentSig);
% Calculating the noise level crossing ratio
for k = 1:length(imf(:,1))
if abs(imf(k,1))<=Vn
imfSum = imfSum + (imf(k,1)^2);
sigSum = sigSum + (currentSig(k)^2);
end
170
==PAGE:196==
E.3. FUNCTIONS
VT/VF Algorithm Implementation
for WARD System
end
NLCR = imfSum/sigSum;
% Defining the first IMF and residue based on the NLCR
if NLCR <= beta
IMF1 = imf(:,1)+imf(:,2);
R = currentSig −IMF1;
else
IMF1 = imf(:,1);
R = currentSig −IMF1 −imf(:,2);
end
% Saving additional data in the struct
EMDData.(databases{db}).(subjectNo).(segmentNo).label = ...
PrepData.(database).(subjectNo).(segmentNo).label;
EMDData.(databases{db}).(subjectNo).(segmentNo).subjectID = ...
PrepData.(database).(subjectNo).(segmentNo).subjectID;
EMDData.(databases{db}).(subjectNo).(segmentNo).featureLabels = ...
PrepData.(database).(subjectNo).(segmentNo).featureLabels;
% Calculating FFTs
signalFFT = fftshift(fft(currentSig));
IMF1FFT = fftshift(fft(IMF1));
RFFT = fftshift(fft(R));
% Calculating the upper envelope
[envUpper, ~] = envelope(currentSig);
% Calculating envelope features
envMean = [];
for b = 1:length(envUpper)/fs
envMean(b) = mean(envUpper(b*fs−(fs−1):b*fs−1));
end
envDiff = diff(envMean);
envDiffMean = mean(envDiff);
envDiffMax = max(envDiff);
envSum = sum(envUpper);
% Calculating acceleration features
accMean = mean(diff(diff(currentSig)));
accMax = max(diff(diff(currentSig)));
accDiff = max(diff(diff(currentSig)))−min(diff(diff(currentSig)));
% Calculating outlier feature
outlierFeat = sum(isoutlier(currentSig,'mean','ThresholdFactor',9));
% Calculating cosine similarity measures and saving features
EMDData.(databases{db}).(subjectNo).(segmentNo).simIMF = ...
cosine_similarity(signalFFT,IMF1FFT);
EMDData.(databases{db}).(subjectNo).(segmentNo).simR = ...
cosine_similarity(signalFFT,RFFT);
EMDData.(databases).(subjectNo).(segmentNo).envDiffMean = envDiffMean;
EMDData.(databases).(subjectNo).(segmentNo).envDiffMax = envDiffMax;
EMDData.(databases).(subjectNo).(segmentNo).envSum = envSum;

for WARD System

EMDData.(databases).(subjectNo).(segmentNo).accMax = accMax;
EMDData.(databases).(subjectNo).(segmentNo).accDiff = accDiff;
EMDData.(databases).(subjectNo).(segmentNo).outlierFeat = outlierFeat;

% Creating label vectors
VTVFLabels = ones(size(VTVFFeatures,1),1);

VTVFTrain = VTVFFeatures(1:floor(0.8*size(VTVFFeatures,1)),:);

trainingLabels = [VTVFTrainLab; nonVTVFTrainLab];

'classification');
% Picking the top 41% most important features
[~, loc] = sort(weights, 'descend');
topFeatures = loc(1:floor((0.41*length(weights))));

% Limiting to the chosen features
chosenVTVFFeatures = VTVFTrain(:,topFeatures);
chosenNonVTVFFeatures = nonVTVFTest(:,topFeatures);
% Upsampling VT/VF using SMOTE
[X1,~,~,~] = smote(chosenVTVFFeatures, 5, 5);
[X2,~,~,~] = smote(X1, 5, 5);
[X3,~,~,~] = smote(X2, 5, 5);
% Collecting non−VT/VF and VT/VF features
chosenFeat = [X3; chosenNonVTVFFeatures];
% Upsampling using SMOTE
chosenLab = [ones(size(X3,1),1); zeros(size(chosenNonVTVFFeatures,1),1)];
[finalTrainFeat,finalTrainLab,~,~] = smote(chosenFeat, [], 5, 'Class',chosenLab);

==PAGE:200==
E.3. FUNCTIONS
VT/VF Algorithm Implementation
for WARD System
%% UPSAMPLING TEST (SMOTE)
% Limiting to the chosen features
chosenVTVFFeatures = VTVFTest(:,topFeatures);
chosenNonVTVFFeatures = nonVTVFTest(:,topFeatures);
% Upsampling VT/VF using SMOTE
[X4,~,~,~] = smote(chosenVTVFFeatures, 3, 5);
[X5,~,~,~] = smote(X4, 5, 5);
[X6,~,~,~] = smote(X5, 5, 5);
% Collecting non−VT/VF and VT/VF features
chosenFeat = [X6; chosenNonVTVFFeatures];
% Upsampling using SMOTE
chosenLab = [ones(size(X6,1),1); zeros(size(chosenNonVTVFFeatures,1),1)];
[finalTestFeat,finalTestLab,~,~] = smote(chosenFeat, [], 5, 'Class',chosenLab);
%% CLASSIFICATION (SVM)
% Training SVM model
SVMModel = fitcsvm(finalTrainFeat,finalTrainLab,...
'KernelFunction','RBF',...
'BoxConstraint',30,'KernelScale',0.68,...
'OptimizeHyperparameters','none',...
'HyperparameterOptimizationOptions',struct('UseParallel',true));
% Classifying using the trained SVM model
ypred = predict(SVMModel,finalTestFeat);
% Calculating performance measures
Performance = classification_performance(ypred, finalTestLab);
% Fitting a posterior probability
[scoreSVMModel, ~] = fitPosterior(SVMModel);
[~, prob] = predict(scoreSVMModel, finalTestFeat);
% Classification thresholds
vec = 0.01:0.01:0.99;
% Iterating through different classification thresholds
for k = 1:length(vec)
% Iterating through observations
for i = 1:length(prob)
if prob(i,1) > vec(k)
% If the posterior probability of belonging to the non−VT/VF class is
% larger than the classification threshold, the prediction is 0
ypredNew(i,1) = 0;
elseif prob(i,2) > vec(end+1−k)
% If the posterior probability of belonging to the VT/VF class is
% larger than the classification threshold, the prediction is 1
ypredNew(i,1) = 1;
end
end

% Calculating performance measures based on the new predictions
newPerformance = classification_performance(ypredNew, finalTestLab);
end

%% VTVF_Algorithm_WARD
%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

function [DataStruct] = loading_ward_all()
%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%
%
% DESCRIPTION: This function loads data from the WARD server.
%
% AUTHORS: Maria L. Sakhat (s154553) & Lena M. Nilsson (s153554)
%
%
% DATE CREATED: 02−12−20
% DATE MODIFIED: 02−12−20
%
%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%
% Set directory to WARD server containing LifeTouch data
cd('/Volumes/department/Sund/Public/WARD/data/dataOut/Lifetouch Setup Mode Samples')
% Define the patient types to load data from
patientTypes = {'gc','brs','bc','rs'};
count = 1;
% Iterate through the number of patient types
for j = 1:length(patientTypes)
d =
dir([patientTypes{j},'*.mat']);
names = fieldnames(d);
subjectName = {d.(names{1})};
% Iterate through the number of subjects
for i = 1:length(subjectName)
% Load the data
data = load(subjectName{i});
if ~isempty(data.dataOut)
% Save the signal and timestamp
signal{count} = (data.dataOut(:,2)/1000)*3.7;
timestamp{count} = data.dataOut(:,1);
count = count + 1;
end
end
end
% Save the variables in a struct
DataStruct.fs = 100;
DataStruct.numberOfSubjects = length(signal);
DataStruct.signal = signal;
DataStruct.timestamp = timestamp;
end

function [Data, fs] = data_segmentation_ward_all()
%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%
%
% DESCRIPTION: This function loads data and divides it into 5 second
%
segments.
%
% OUTPUT:
%
o Data: Struct containing each data segment for each record for each
%
subject
%
.(subjectNo): ID of the subject
%
.(recNo): ID of the 10 second recording
%
.(segmentNo): ID of the segment
%
.signal: The signal for the segment
%
.subjectID: The subject ID for the segment
%
o fs: Sampling frequency
%
% AUTHORS: Maria L. Sakhat (s154553) & Lena M. Nilsson (s153554)
%
%
% DATE CREATED: 02−12−20
% DATE MODIFIED: 02−12−20
%
%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%
%% DATA SEGMENTATION
%% LOAD DATA
DataStruct = loading_ward_all();
%% UNWRAP VARIABLES
signal = DataStruct.signal;
timestamp = DataStruct.timestamp;
fs = DataStruct.fs;
numberOfSubjects = DataStruct.numberOfSubjects;
%% CREATE SEGMENTS
segmentLength = 5; % Seconds
windowSize = segmentLength*fs;
windowShift =
1*fs;
b = seconds(30); % Split time
for i = 1:numberOfSubjects
subjectNo = sprintf('subject%d',i);
% Divide into 10 second recordings
t = datetime(timestamp{i},'ConvertFrom','datenum');
t2 = datetime(t,'InputFormat','dd.MM.yyyy HH:mm:ss');
dt = diff(t2);
% Find splits larger than the split time
splitlocs = [0; find(dt>b)];
countRec = 1;
% Iterate through the number of records
178
==PAGE:204==
E.4. VERIFICATION
VT/VF Algorithm Implementation
for WARD System
for l = 1:length(splitlocs)−1
recNo = sprintf('rec%d',countRec);
count = 1;
countOld = count;
startIdx = 1;
endIdx = windowSize;
actualSignal = signal{i}(splitlocs(l)+1:splitlocs(l+1));
% Loop through all possible segments in the signal
while endIdx<=length(actualSignal)
segmentNo = sprintf('seg%d',count);
% Exclude NaNs
if sum(isnan(actualSignal(startIdx:endIdx,1)))==0
Data.(subjectNo).(recNo).(segmentNo).subjectID = i;
Data.(subjectNo).(recNo).(segmentNo).signal = ...
actualSignal(startIdx:endIdx,1);
count = count+1;
end
% Move the window
startIdx = startIdx + windowShift;
endIdx = startIdx + windowSize−1;
end
if count > countOld
countRec = countRec + 1;
end
end
end
end

function [PrepData] = preprocessing_ward_all(Data, fs)
%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%
%
% DESCRIPTION: This function performs preprocessing of the signal segments.
%
% INPUT:
%
o Data: Struct containing each data segment for each record for each
%
subject
%
.(subjectNo): ID of the subject
%
.(recNo): ID of the 10 second recording
%
.(segmentNo): ID of the segment
%
.signal: The signal for the segment
%
.subjectID: The subject ID for the segment
%
o fs: Sampling frequency
%
% OUTPUT:
%
o PrepData: Struct containing each data segment for each record for each
%
subject after preprocessing
%
.(subjectNo): ID of the subject
179
==PAGE:205==
E.4. VERIFICATION
VT/VF Algorithm Implementation
for WARD System
%
.(recNo): ID of the record
%
.(segmentNo): ID of the segment
%
.signal: The signal for the segment
%
.subjectID: The subject ID for the segment
%
% AUTHORS: Maria L. Sakhat (s154553) & Lena M. Nilsson (s153554)

% DATE MODIFIED: 04−12−20
%
%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%
%% DEFINE FILTERS
highpassFreq = 1;
lowpassFreq = 20;
lowpassOrder = 12;
highpassOrder = 1;
nyquist = 0.5*fs;
[bH,aH] = butter(highpassOrder, highpassFreq/nyquist, 'high');
[bL,aL] = butter(lowpassOrder, lowpassFreq/nyquist, 'low');
%% PREPROCESSING
% Iterate through the subjects
for i = 1:numel(fieldnames(Data))
subjectNo = sprintf('subject%d',i);
% Iterate through the records
for k = 1:numel(fieldnames(Data.(subjectNo)))
recNo = sprintf('rec%d',k);
% Iterate through the segments
for j = 1:numel(fieldnames(Data.(subjectNo).(recNo)))
segmentNo = sprintf('seg%d',j);
% Subtraction of mean
PrepData.(subjectNo).(recNo).(segmentNo).signal = ...
(Data.(subjectNo).(recNo).(segmentNo).signal −...
mean(Data.(subjectNo).(recNo).(segmentNo).signal))/...
std(Data.(subjectNo).(recNo).(segmentNo).signal);
% Moving average filter
PrepData.(subjectNo).(recNo).(segmentNo).signal = ...
movmean(Data.(subjectNo).(recNo).(segmentNo).signal,5);
% High−pass filter
PrepData.(subjectNo).(recNo).(segmentNo).signal = ...
filter(bH,aH,Data.(subjectNo).(recNo).(segmentNo).signal);
% Low−pass filter
PrepData.(subjectNo).(recNo).(segmentNo).signal = ...
filter(bL,aL,Data.(subjectNo).(recNo).(segmentNo).signal);
% Adding definitions to the struct
PrepData.(subjectNo).(recNo).(segmentNo).subjectID = ...

VT/VF Algorithm Implementation
for WARD System
Data.(subjectNo).(recNo).(segmentNo).subjectID;
end
end

function [EMDData] = feature_extraction_ward_all(PrepData)
%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%
%
% DESCRIPTION: This function computes the EMD and DFT of each segment of
%
data, and then extracts features using cosine similarity
%
measure. Additional features are also computed.
%
% INPUT:
%
o PrepData: Struct containing each data segment for each record for each
%
subject after preprocessing
%
.(subjectNo): ID of the subject
%
.(recNo): ID of the record
%
.(segmentNo): ID of the segment
%
.signal: The signal for the segment
%
.subjectID: The subject ID for the segment
%
% OUTPUT:
%
o EMDData: Struct containing each data segment for each record for each
%
subject after preprocessing
%
.(subjectNo): ID of the subject
%
.(recNo): ID of the record
%
.(segmentNo): ID of the segment
%
.subjectID: The subject ID for the segment
%
.simIMF: Similarity measure of DFT of the signal and
%
DFT of IMF
%
.simR: Similarity measure of DFT of the signal and
%
DFT of residue
%
.envDiffMean: Mean of a differentiated vector
%
consisting of five mean envelope
%
values of each second
%
.envDiffMax: Maximum of a differentiated vector
%
consisting of five mean envelope
%
values of each second
%
.envSum: Sum of the upper envelope
%
.accMean: Mean of an acceleration vector
%
.accMax: Maximum of an acceleration vector
%
.accDiff: Difference between the maximum and minimum
%
of an acceleration vector
%
.outlierFeat: Number of outliers in a segment
%
% AUTHORS: Maria L. Sakhat (s154553) & Lena M. Nilsson (s153554)
%
%
% DATE CREATED: 04−12−20
% DATE MODIFIED: 04−01−21
181
==PAGE:207==
E.4. VERIFICATION
VT/VF Algorithm Implementation
for WARD System
%
%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%
%% FEATURE EXTRACTION
% Defining parameters
alpha = 0.05;
beta = 0.02;
% Performing EMD for every segment
% Iterating through the subjects
for i = 1:numel(fieldnames(PrepData))
subjectNo = sprintf('subject%d',i);
% Iterating through the 10−second records
for k = 1:numel(fieldnames(PrepData.(subjectNo)))
recNo = sprintf('rec%d',k);
% Iterating through the segments
for j = 1:numel(fieldnames(PrepData.(subjectNo).(recNo)))
segmentNo = sprintf('seg%d',j);
currentSig = PrepData.(subjectNo).(recNo).(segmentNo).signal;
imfSum = 0;
sigSum = 0;
% Performing EMD
[imf, ~] = emd(currentSig, 'Display', 0);
% Calculating the noise level
Vn = alpha*max(currentSig);
% Calculating the noise level crossing ratio
for k = 1:length(imf(:,1))
if abs(imf(k,1))<=Vn
imfSum = imfSum + (imf(k,1)^2);
sigSum = sigSum + (currentSig(k)^2);
end
end
NLCR = imfSum/sigSum;
% Defining the first IMF and residue based on the NLCR
if NLCR <= beta
IMF1 = imf(:,1)+imf(:,2);
R = currentSig −IMF1;
else
IMF1 = imf(:,1);
R = currentSig −IMF1 −imf(:,2);
end
% Saving additional data in the struct
EMDData.(subjectNo).(recNo).(segmentNo).subjectID = ...
PrepData.(subjectNo).(recNo).(segmentNo).subjectID;
% Calculating FFTs
signalFFT = fftshift(fft(currentSig));
IMF1FFT = fftshift(fft(IMF1));
RFFT = fftshift(fft(R));

==PAGE:208==
E.4. VERIFICATION
VT/VF Algorithm Implementation
for WARD System
% Calculating the upper envelope
[envUpper, ~] = envelope(currentSig);
% Calculating envelope features
envMean = [];
for b = 1:length(envUpper)/fs
envMean(b) = mean(envUpper(b*fs−(fs−1):b*fs−1));
end
envDiff = diff(envMean);
envDiffMean = mean(envDiff);
envDiffMax = max(envDiff);
envSum = sum(envUpper);
% Calculating acceleration features
accMean = mean(diff(diff(currentSig)));
accMax = max(diff(diff(currentSig)));
accDiff = max(diff(diff(currentSig)))−min(diff(diff(currentSig)));
% Calculating outlier feature
outlierFeat = sum(isoutlier(currentSig,'mean','ThresholdFactor',9));
% Calculating cosine similarity measures and saving features
EMDData.(subjectNo).(recNo).(segmentNo).simIMF = ...
cosine_similarity(signalFFT,IMF1FFT);
EMDData.(subjectNo).(recNo).(segmentNo).simR = ...
cosine_similarity(signalFFT,RFFT);
EMDData.(subjectNo).(recNo).(segmentNo).envDiffMean = envDiffMean;
EMDData.(subjectNo).(recNo).(segmentNo).envDiffMax = envDiffMax;
EMDData.(subjectNo).(recNo).(segmentNo).envSum = envSum;
EMDData.(subjectNo).(recNo).(segmentNo).accMean = accMean;
EMDData.(subjectNo).(recNo).(segmentNo).accMax = accMax;

function [predictions] = classification_ward_all(scoreSVMModel, topFeatures, EMDData)
%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%
%
% DESCRIPTION: This function performs classification with an SVM classifier.
%
% INPUT:
%
o EMDData: Struct containing each data segment for each record for each
%
subject after preprocessing
%
.(subjectNo): ID of the subject
%
.(recNo): ID of the record
183

E.4. VERIFICATION
VT/VF Algorithm Implementation
for WARD System
%
.(segmentNo): ID of the segment
%
.subjectID: The subject ID for the segment
%
.simIMF: Similarity measure of DFT of the signal and
%
DFT of IMF
%
.simR: Similarity measure of DFT of the signal and
%
DFT of residue
%
.envDiffMean: Mean of a differentiated vector
%
consisting of five mean envelope
%
values of each second
%
.envDiffMax: Maximum of a differentiated vector
%
consisting of five mean envelope
%
values of each second
%
.envSum: Sum of the upper envelope
%
.accMean: Mean of an acceleration vector
%
.accMax: Maximum of an acceleration vector
%
.accDiff: Difference between the maximum and minimum
%
of an acceleration vector
%
.outlierFeat: Number of outliers in a segment
%
o scoreSVMModel: Trained SVM model used for classification
%
o topFeatures: Features selected from feature selection
%
% OUTPUT:
%
o predictions: Vector of output predictions of the model
%
% AUTHORS: Maria L. Sakhat (s154553) & Lena M. Nilsson (s153554)
%
%
% DATE CREATED: 04−12−20
% DATE MODIFIED: 18−01−21
%
%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%
%% CLASSIFICATION (SVM)
% Preallocation
predictions = zeros(1,42589); % gc
% predictions = zeros(1,131839); % brs
% Counter
count = 1;
% Iterating through the subjects
for i = 1:numel(fieldnames(EMDData))
subjectNo = sprintf('subject%d',i)
% Iterating through the records
for k = 1:numel(fieldnames(EMDData.(subjectNo)))
recNo = sprintf('rec%d',k);
% Iterating through the segments
for j = 1:numel(fieldnames(EMDData.(subjectNo).(recNo)))
features = zeros(numel(fieldnames(EMDData.(subjectNo).(recNo))),1007);
segmentNo = sprintf('seg%d',j);
% Unpack features
newFeatures = [EMDData.(subjectNo).(recNo).(segmentNo).simIMF; ...
EMDData.(subjectNo).(recNo).(segmentNo).simR;...
EMDData.(subjectNo).(recNo).(segmentNo).envDiffMean; ...
EMDData.(subjectNo).(recNo).(segmentNo).envDiffMax; ...
184
==PAGE:210==
E.4. VERIFICATION
VT/VF Algorithm Implementation
for WARD System
EMDData.(subjectNo).(recNo).(segmentNo).envSum; ...
EMDData.(subjectNo).(recNo).(segmentNo).accMean; ...
EMDData.(subjectNo).(recNo).(segmentNo).accMax; ...
EMDData.(subjectNo).(recNo).(segmentNo).accDiff; ...
EMDData.(subjectNo).(recNo).(segmentNo).outlierFeat]';
% Concatenate features
features(j,:) = newFeatures;
end
% Classify the segments in the record
[~, featP] = predict(scoreSVMModel,features(:,topFeatures));
% Majority vote principle
if length(find(featP(:,2)>(1−0.43)))> length(find(featP(:,1)>=0.43))
% 100% VT/VF principle
% if length(find(featP(:,2)>(1−0.43))) == length(featP)
% If more than 50% of the segments in the record are classified
% as VT/VF with a probability of more than 57%, the record is VT/VF
newPred = 1;
else
% If 50% or more of the segments in the record are classified
% as non−VT/VF with a probability of 43% or more, the record
% is non−VT/VF
newPred = 0;
end
% The prediction is saved
predictions(count) = newPred;
% Update counter
count = count + 1;
end
end
% Remove exceeding preallocations
predictions = predictions(1:count−1);
end
E.4.2.6
Evaluation Plots
function [] = plots_for_evaluation(predictions, Data)
%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%
%
% DESCRIPTION: This function plots two to four 10−second signals per subject,
%
one or two that are classified as VT/VF, and one or two that
%
are classified as non−VT/VF, given that such a 10−second
%
signal exists for the subject. The plots are saved both with
%
and without labels. A maximum of 100 plots of each kind is saved.
%
% INPUT:
%
o predictions: The output predictions of the model
%
o Data: Struct containing each data segment for each subject for each
%
database
%
.(subjectNo): ID of the subject
%
.(recNo): ID of the 10 second recording
%
.(segmentNo): ID of the segment
%
.signal: The signal for the segment
%
.subjectID: The subject ID for the segment

==PAGE:211==
E.4. VERIFICATION
VT/VF Algorithm Implementation
for WARD System
%
% AUTHORS: Maria L. Sakhat (s154553) & Lena M. Nilsson (s153554)
%
%
% DATE CREATED: 04−01−21
% DATE MODIFIED: 25−01−21
%
%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%
%% PLOTS FOR EVALUATION
databases = {'rs','bc', 'brs', 'gc'};
numberOfEach = [16, 16, 40, 28];
% Number of subjects
numberOfSubjects = length(fieldnames(Data));
% Sampling frequency
fs = 100;
% Counter
count = 0;
% Path to the folder the figures should be saved in
folderPath = ['/Users/lenamnilsson/Documents/Universitetet_2/Kandidat/'...,
'Master_Thesis/Danmarks Tekniske Universitet/Maria Emilie Loft Sakhat',...
' −Master Thesis/MATLAB/WARD_arr/EvaluationSignals/'];
% Iterate through subjects
for j = 1:numberOfSubjects
subjectNo = sprintf('subject%d',j);
% Counters
saveCountVTVF = 1;
saveCountNonVTVF = 1;
% Iterate through 10−sec recordings
for i = 1:length(fieldnames(Data.(subjectNo)))
recNo = sprintf('rec%d',i);
% Iterate through 5−second segments
if length(fieldnames(Data.(subjectNo).(recNo)))>2
for k = 1:length(fieldnames(Data.(subjectNo).(recNo)))
segmentNo = sprintf('seg%d',k);
% Concatenate segments to constitute the full 10−second signal
if k == 1
fullSig = Data.(subjectNo).(recNo).(segmentNo).signal;
else
fullSig = [fullSig; ...
Data.(subjectNo).(recNo).(segmentNo).signal(end−fs+1:end)];
end
end
% If the segment is classified as VT/VF
if predictions(i) == 1
% Save the signal
signal.(subjectNo){saveCountVTVF} = fullSig;
% Update counter
saveCountVTVF = saveCountVTVF+1;
% If the segment is classified as non−VT/VF

E.4. VERIFICATION
VT/VF Algorithm Implementation
for WARD System
elseif predictions(i) == 0
% Save the signal
signalN.(subjectNo){saveCountNonVTVF} = fullSig;
% Update counter
saveCountNonVTVF = saveCountNonVTVF+1;
end
end
end
end
% The number of subjects containing VT/VF segments
subjectNamesVTVF = fieldnames(signal);
% Limit to a maximum of 100 VTVF signals
if length(subjectNamesVTVF) > 100
ps = randperm(length(subjectNamesVTVF));
subjectNamesVTVF = subjectNamesVTVF(ps(1:100));
end
% The number of subjects containing non−VT/VF segments
subjectNamesNonVTVF = fieldnames(signalN);
% Limit to a maximum of 100 non−VTVF signals
if length(subjectNamesNonVTVF) > 100
pns = randperm(length(subjectNamesNonVTVF));
subjectNamesNonVTVF = subjectNamesNonVTVF(pns(1:100));
end
% Choose one or two VT/VF segment per subject and save the signals
countVTVF = 1;
for h = 1:length(subjectNamesVTVF)
idx = randi(length(signal.(subjectNamesVTVF{h})));
idx2 = randi(length(signal.(subjectNamesVTVF{h})));
% If more than one signal exists
if length(signal.(subjectNamesVTVF{h})) > 1
% Ensure that the same index is not chosen twice
while idx == idx2
idx2 = randi(length(signal.(subjectNamesVTVF{h})));
end
% Save two signals
fullSigVTVF{countVTVF} = signal.(subjectNamesVTVF{h}){idx};
fullSigVTVF{countVTVF+1} = signal.(subjectNamesVTVF{h}){idx2};
countVTVF = countVTVF+2;
% If only one signal exists
else
% Save one signal
fullSigVTVF{countVTVF} = signal.(subjectNamesVTVF{h}){idx};
countVTVF = countVTVF+1;
end
end
% Choose one or two non−VT/VF segment per subject and save the signals
countNonVTVF = 1;
for l = 1:length(subjectNamesNonVTVF)
idx = randi(length(signalN.(subjectNamesNonVTVF{l})));
idx2 = randi(length(signalN.(subjectNamesNonVTVF{l})));
% If more than one signal exists

if length(signalN.(subjectNamesNonVTVF{l})) > 1
% Ensure that the same index is not chosen twice

idx2 = randi(length(signalN.(subjectNamesNonVTVF{l})));
end
% Save two signals
fullSigNVTVF{countNonVTVF} = signalN.(subjectNamesNonVTVF{l}){idx};
fullSigNVTVF{countNonVTVF+1} = signalN.(subjectNamesNonVTVF{l}){idx2};
countNonVTVF = countNonVTVF + 2;
% If only one signal exists
else
% Save one signal
fullSigNVTVF{countNonVTVF} = signalN.(subjectNamesNonVTVF{l}){idx};
countNonVTVF = countNonVTVF + 1;
end
end
%%
% Create label vector
labelVec = [ones(length(fullSigVTVF),1); zeros(length(fullSigNVTVF),1)];
% Combining the two signal vectors
fullSig = [fullSigVTVF'; fullSigNVTVF'];
% Shuffling the order
p = randperm(length(fullSig));
fullSig = fullSig(p);
labelVec = labelVec(p);
% Initialize counter
countPlot = 1;
for h = 1:length(fullSig)
% Initialize figure
fig = figure(1);
subplot(3,1,countPlot)
set(fig,'Units','normalized');
set(fig,'Position',[0.05 0.3 0.92 0.9]);
% Plot the signal and an appertaining time vector
plot(linspace(0,length(fullSig{h})/fs,length(fullSig{h})),fullSig{h})
ylim([5 10]);
xlabel('Time [s]','FontSize',16)
ylabel('Amplitude','FontSize',16)
% Update counter
countPlot = countPlot + 1;
% Limit to 3 subplots per page
if countPlot == 4
% Save the figure without annotations
print([folderPath,'verification',num2str(h)],'−dpdf','−bestfit')
% Add the labels to the figure
title(fig.Children(1),labelVec(h))
title(fig.Children(2),labelVec(h−1))
title(fig.Children(3),labelVec(h−2))
% Save the figure with annotations

print([folderPath,'ann_verification',num2str(h)],'−dpdf','−bestfit')
% Close the figure and restart counter
close all
countPlot = 1;
% Enable the last page if the number of plots is not divisible by 3
elseif h == length(fullSig)
% Save the figure without annotations
print([folderPath,'verification',num2str(h)],'−dpdf','−bestfit')
% Add the labels to the figure
title(fig.Children(1),labelVec(h))
try
title(fig.Children(2),labelVec(h−1))
catch
end
% Save the figure with annotations
print([folderPath,'ann_verification',num2str(h)],'−dpdf','−bestfit')
% Close the figure and restart counter
close all
countPlot = 1;
end
end
end
